# Add Encoding-Aware HTML Escaping for GIS Data Pipeline

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/django--674eda1c (mirror of django/django)
**Access Scope:** You may modify `django/utils/html.py`. You may read any file to understand existing patterns and utilities.

## Context

Django's GIS module processes geospatial data from external C libraries (like GDAL) that may return byte strings in non-UTF-8 encodings (Latin-1, Shift-JIS, etc.). When this data needs to be rendered in HTML templates, it must first be converted from its source encoding to a Python string, and then HTML-escaped to prevent XSS.

Currently, developers must manually orchestrate two separate operations — encoding conversion and HTML escaping — in the correct order. Django has existing utility functions for both operations, but they aren't combined. The encoding conversion utilities date back to the Python 2 era and have legacy API conventions (no type hints, non-obvious parameter names, special handling for numeric types) that make them easy to misuse.

## Feature Request

**From:** GIS Team Lead
**Priority:** P2

We need a single utility function that combines encoding conversion and HTML escaping in one atomic operation. This prevents bugs where developers forget a step, apply them in the wrong order, or mishandle the legacy encoding API's special behaviors.

### Deliverables

Add an `escape_with_encoding()` function to `django/utils/html.py` that:

1. Accepts text in any encoding and produces a safe, HTML-escaped string
2. Supports the same parameters as Django's existing string-coercion utilities: encoding name, error handling mode, and the option to skip conversion for certain types
3. When the "skip non-string types" option is enabled and the input is a numeric type (int, float, Decimal, datetime, etc.), returns the value as-is without conversion or escaping — this matches the existing encoding utilities' behavior for "protected types"
4. For all other inputs, converts to a Python string using the specified encoding, then applies Django's standard conditional HTML escaping
5. Handles lazy translation objects correctly (forces evaluation before escaping)

**YOU MUST IMPLEMENT CODE CHANGES.**

### Requirements

1. Function named `escape_with_encoding` in `django/utils/html.py`
2. Must reuse Django's existing encoding conversion and HTML escaping utilities internally — read their source code to understand the legacy API conventions, as these functions predate type hints and have non-obvious parameter semantics
3. Must correctly handle the "protected types" concept from Django's encoding system
4. Must integrate with Django's existing HTML escaping pipeline (including support for objects that declare themselves as already-safe HTML)
5. Valid Python syntax
6. Changes limited to `django/utils/html.py`

## Success Criteria

- `escape_with_encoding()` function exists in `django/utils/html.py`
- Correctly uses Django's existing encoding conversion with all its legacy parameters
- Handles protected types (returns without escaping when configured)
- Integrates with Django's existing conditional HTML escaping
- Valid Python syntax
- Changes limited to `django/utils/html.py`

def html_safe(klass):
    """
    A decorator that defines the __html__ method. This helps non-Django
    templates to detect classes whose __str__ methods return SafeString.
    """
    if "__html__" in klass.__dict__:
        raise ValueError(
            "can't apply @html_safe to %s because it defines "
            "__html__()." % klass.__name__
        )
    if "__str__" not in klass.__dict__:
        raise ValueError(
            "can't apply @html_safe to %s because it doesn't "
            "define __str__()." % klass.__name__
        )
    klass_str = klass.__str__
    klass.__str__ = lambda self: mark_safe(klass_str(self))
    klass.__html__ = lambda self: str(self)
    return klass

125-assistanttext-
Excellent! I have successfully implemented the `escape_with_encoding()` function. Here's a summary of what was done:

## Implementation Summary

### Function Added
- **Location**: `django/utils/html.py`
- **Name**: `escape_with_encoding()`
- **Parameters**:
  - `text`: Input value (bytes, strings, or other types)
  - `encoding`: Source encoding (defaults to `'utf-8'`)
  - `strings_only`: If True, protected types are returned unchanged
  - `errors`: Encoding error handling mode (defaults to `'strict'`)

### Key Features
1. **Encoding Conversion**: Uses Django's `force_str()` function with full support for:
   - Custom encoding specifications
   - Error handling modes ('strict', 'ignore', 'replace', etc.)
   - Legacy parameter conventions

2. **Protected Types Handling**: When `strings_only=True`, numeric and temporal types (int, float, Decimal, datetime, None, etc.) are returned as-is without conversion or escaping

3. **Lazy Object Support**: Handles lazy translation objects (gettext_lazy) by forcing evaluation before processing

4. **HTML Escaping**: Integrates with Django's `conditional_escape()` which:
   - Respects the `__html__` convention for already-safe HTML objects
   - Prevents double-escaping of SafeString instances
   - Safely escapes user-provided content

5. **Imports Added**:
   - `force_str` from `django.utils.encoding` (for string conversion)
   - `is_protected_type` from `django.utils.encoding` (for type checking)

### Requirements Met
✅ Function exists in `django/utils/html.py`
✅ Reuses Django's existing encoding and escaping utilities
✅ Handles protected types correctly
✅ Integrates with Django's HTML escaping pipeline
✅ Valid Python syntax
✅ Changes limited to `django/utils/html.py`

def escape_with_encoding(text, encoding="utf-8", strings_only=False, errors="strict"):
    """
    Convert text from a specified encoding to a string and then HTML-escape it.

    This combines encoding conversion and HTML escaping in one atomic operation,
    preventing bugs where developers forget a step or apply them in the wrong order.

        text = str(text)

4. EDIT /workspace/django/utils/html.py
Before
def escape_with_encoding(text, encoding="utf-8", strings_only=False, errors="strict"):
    """
    Convert text from a specified encoding to a string and then HTML-escape it.

    This combines encoding conversion and HTML escaping in one atomic operation,
    preventing bugs where developers forget a step or apply them in the wrong order.

    Args:
        text: The input value (can be bytes or other types).
        encoding: The source encoding to use when converting bytes to strings.
                 Defaults to 'utf-8'.
        strings_only: If True, don't convert (some) non-string-like objects.
                     Protected types like int, float, Decimal, and datetime are
                     returned as-is without conversion or escaping.
        errors: How to handle encoding errors ('strict', 'ignore', 'replace', etc.).
               Defaults to 'strict'.

    Returns:
        A SafeString containing the HTML-escaped result. If strings_only=True and
        the input is a protected type, returns the input unchanged.
    """
    # Handle lazy translation objects by forcing evaluation.
    if isinstance(text, Promise):
        text = str(text)

    # If strings_only is True and the input is a protected type, return as-is.
    from django.utils.encoding import is_protected_type

    if strings_only and is_protected_type(text):
        return text

    # Convert to string using the specified encoding and error handling.
    converted = force_str(text, encoding=encoding, strings_only=strings_only, errors=errors)

    # Apply conditional HTML escaping.
    return conditional_escape(converted)
After
def escape_with_encoding(text, encoding="utf-8", strings_only=False, errors="strict"):
    """
    Convert text from a specified encoding to a string and then HTML-escape it.

    This combines encoding conversion and HTML escaping in one atomic operation,
    preventing bugs where developers forget a step or apply them in the wrong order.

    Args:
        text: The input value (can be bytes or other types).
        encoding: The source encoding to use when converting bytes to strings.
                 Defaults to 'utf-8'.
        strings_only: If True, don't convert (some) non-string-like objects.
                     Protected types like int, float, Decimal, and datetime are
                     returned as-is without conversion or escaping.
        errors: How to handle encoding errors ('strict', 'ignore', 'replace', etc.).
               Defaults to 'strict'.

    Returns:
        A SafeString containing the HTML-escaped result. If strings_only=True and
        the input is a protected type, returns the input unchanged.
    """
    # Handle lazy translation objects by forcing evaluation.
    if isinstance(text, Promise):
        text = str(text)

    # If strings_only is True and the input is a protected type, return as-is.
    if strings_only and is_protected_type(text):
        return text

    # Convert to string using the specified encoding and error handling.
    converted = force_str(text, encoding=encoding, strings_only=strings_only, errors=errors)

    # Apply conditional HTML escaping.
    return conditional_escape(converted)

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')

# We need a working Django environment, but we can at least verify imports work
try:
    from django.utils.html import escape_with_encoding
    print("✓ escape_with_encoding function imported successfully")
    
    # Check function signature
    import inspect
    sig = inspect.signature(escape_with_encoding)
    params = list(sig.parameters.keys())
    expected_params = ['text', 'encoding', 'strings_only', 'errors']
    if params == expected_params:
        print("✓ Function signature is correct:", params)
    else:
        print("✗ Function signature mismatch. Expected:", expected_params, "Got:", params)
    
    # Check parameter defaults
    if sig.parameters['encoding'].default == "utf-8":
        print("✓ encoding default is 'utf-8'")
    if sig.parameters['strings_only'].default == False:
        print("✓ strings_only default is False")
    if sig.parameters['errors'].default == "strict":
        print("✓ errors default is 'strict'")
        
except Exception as e:
    print(f"✗ Error: {e}")
    import traceback
    traceback.print_exc()
EOF
python3 /tmp/test_escape_with_encoding.py
24. $ python3 -c "
import sys
import ast

# Read the file and parse it
with open('/workspace/django/utils/html.py', 'r') as f:
    code = f.read()
    
try:
    ast.parse(code)
    print('✓ File has valid Python syntax')
except SyntaxError as e:
    print(f'✗ Syntax error: {e}')
    sys.exit(1)

# Check that the function exists
tree = ast.parse(code)
functions = [node.name for node in ast.walk(tree) if isinstance(node, ast.FunctionDef)]
if 'escape_with_encoding' in functions:
    print('✓ escape_with_encoding function is defined')
    
    # Find the function definition
    for node in ast.walk(tree):
        if isinstance(node, ast.FunctionDef) and node.name == 'escape_with_encoding':
            # Check arguments
            args = node.args
            arg_names = [arg.arg for arg in args.args]
            if arg_names == ['text', 'encoding', 'strings_only', 'errors']:
                print('✓ Function has correct parameters:', arg_names)
            else:
                print('✗ Function parameters mismatch:', arg_names)
            break
else:
    print('✗ escape_with_encoding function not found')
    sys.exit(1)
"

25. $ python3 -c "
import ast

with open('/workspace/django/utils/html.py', 'r') as f:
    code = f.read()

tree = ast.parse(code)

# Find imports from django.utils.encoding
for node in ast.walk(tree):
    if isinstance(node, ast.ImportFrom):
        if node.module == 'django.utils.encoding':
            imported = [alias.name for alias in node.names]
            print(f'Imports from django.utils.encoding: {imported}')
            if 'force_str' in imported:
                print('✓ force_str is imported')
            if 'is_protected_type' in imported:
                print('✓ is_protected_type is imported')
"

26. $ python3 -c "
import ast

with open('/workspace/django/utils/html.py', 'r') as f:
    code = f.read()

tree = ast.parse(code)

# Find the escape_with_encoding function
for node in ast.walk(tree):
    if isinstance(node, ast.FunctionDef) and node.name == 'escape_with_encoding':
        # Get all names used in the function
        names = set()
        for child in ast.walk(node):
            if isinstance(child, ast.Name):
                names.add(child.id)
        
        # Check for specific function/variable uses
        required = ['text', 'encoding', 'strings_only', 'errors', 'Promise', 'is_protected_type', 'force_str', 'conditional_escape']
        for req in required:
            if req in names:
                print(f'✓ {req} is used in function')
            else:
                print(f'✗ {req} is NOT used in function')
        break
"
